In answer to those who argue that the prophecy of the 'prince that was promised' was ignored in GOT, it wasn't ignored at all, because it was indeed a 'prince' promised, not a King. John was not meant to be King. As to the argument that Ayra Stark's defeat of the Night King was unexpected and not foreshadowed, or course it WAS foreshadowed in the many (too mnay) episodes concerning her training as a faceless assassin in Bravos, not to mention her ownership of the very same Valerian steel dagger once owned by Peter Baylish, used in an attempt on murdering Bran, and featuring now in House of The Dragon. Same dagger in case no one noticed. The two shows tie in with each other and some things that seemed to have made no sense in 'Thones' will make more sense now. Both shows are brilliant.

This makes me once again enthralled by/with the ever-evolving imagination that we, as human beings - in so many infinite aspects - possess; and continue to progress. I was truly heartbroken, angry, bewildered, shocked (in an indescribably negative sense), & resigned myself - once again - to fully enveloping myself in the books, & the dastardly hope that G.R.R.M. would/will actually & TRULY complete ASOIAF so that all could be bring the majesty of this franchise/World to a JUST, SENSIBLE, HASHED-OUT, ENTHRALLING way.    But, My God, I hope I am not prematurely (& yes, more or less, based on this trailer, alone) excitedly re-investing myself into cinematic version of this seemingly-endless, beautifully-written - into what's unfolded into a true literary work-of-art; Exploring every & all senses, emotions, being both terrified, enthralled, & elated with the turning of each & every page.    In all honesty... it isn't/wasn't even the trailer in it's entirety; But (and TRULY DIE-HARD fans will surely appreciate this - as much as I...) when I got the first glance of His Grace's hand on the arm of the throne; THEN to furthermore grab a glance of House of the Dragon's version of the Iron Throne, in comparison to the horribly, almost mockingly-done version in AGOT - that there - for me - was enough of a hope that this series may just capture the TRUE essence of what it always meant to.  *Fingers crossed, & any & all wood in my vicinity has been knocked on*  ...Let us hope we can rejoice - once again - in what the initial half of AGOT accomplished; and that the passion for the story, & World (in it's entirety) that was - at 1st captured - only to be haphazardly, & disrespectfully-abandoned by D&D - will INSTEAD - ring true initially AND throughout H.O.T.D. - from the 1st scene - to the very last; Reinstalling my faith in cinematic storytelling.

*semi-productive procrastination*  (noun) When you're doing work that's not the work you should be doing, but instead of just procrastinating you're being semi-productive and doing something that's not really important but still relates to your task.also: (verb) to semi-productively procrastinateSimilar to pro-crastination, but not nearly as productive. I love that the dragons looks individual from each other, unlike in GoT where they exactly look the same just with different colors. Here in HoTD each dragons has its own facial features and facial structures and different body structures, u can really identify one from another. Also they redesigned the dragons to be more biologically plausible. They extended the wings to go down to the base of the tail, cos in reality the legs and tail will droop downwards if theres no membrane there to catch air and lift the legs and tail.  In GoT the dragon wings only went down the dragon's waist, which is biologically wrong cos the rear part of the dragon will droop down when it flies real life per se. I love that detail. Also the flying animations improved, very bat-like wing flapping cosnthats how membrane wings actually move in real life.  Edit: i just realized, The iron throne will gradually lose those swords as the show progresses, which will lead to the iron throne we saw in Game of Thrones. The gradual losing of swords of the throne is also a metaphor of the targaryens slowly losing their grip on power and dominance and then they will get overthrown by the kingslayer jaime and the Baratheons, which is the beginning of Game of Thrones season 1.
